de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or a stone, or something similar like iron; or seeds, such as peas, beans; or something flowing, like water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, whether a pebble or something else that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in it, one must hold the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	It often comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then proceed to extract it with fine forceps, according to its shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out through the pincers, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a slender needle of small tubing; and if it does not come out in this way, make an iron hook and push the hook's tip into the ear canal firmly, and plug around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out forcefully, for often it will come out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take bird glue, and put some on a tool designed for this purpose, and place a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the pebble or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to split the ear so that pus comes out, and a spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first make the patient's head bleed, and draw blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small split in the root of the ear at the fat where it depends; and the split should be like a crescent moon, so that you can reach the pebble, then extract it according to your ability, and suck on it vigorously with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains which are there and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatulum with a thin needle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.

s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it jumps out by itself, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if not, take many small stones according to the length of your index finger and heat them gently in the fire; then place one of these heated stones into the ear of the sufferer, and press down on it with another stone from above, and insert a third stone into the ear from below; and keep placing heated stones over the affected area until all the ache has subsided, and thus will all the pain subside; and if you see fit, take a straw, and place one end in the ear, and heat the other end in the fire until the most painful part is scorched; then repeat this process with other straws until all the pain goes away, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the worm, if it is small like a flea or similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest way to remove what is in the ear.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ear; and the same thing happens to adults due to an abscess or wound inside the ear, and sometimes this abscess erupts in the ear, which cannot be seen; and sometimes there is only a small opening, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When it erupts and cannot be seen, it indicates a poor prognosis in many cases, and in such cases, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane exposed, then it has reached this stage due to the following reasons:

de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ointment comes in papers when they are moist and dry; you should therefore extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the root of a spatula; then place powdered vitriol on the site.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not removed by scraping, then cauterize them with a delicate lens-shaped cautery tool, and the cautery after the incision is beneficial; they often reappear when something remains in their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times they come with paper-thin things that look like gravel in appearance and hardness, and this is why this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of thick moisture on top and bottom; the treatment is as follows: examine if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and it is an easy matter to know; then cut it open from the side, then carefully peel off the outer layer from each part, then pick it up with tweezers, and scoop it out.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot scoop it out without piercing the eardrum, do not harm the patient; and if the fissure is large, stitch it up, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not use force, as the ointment will restore it right away and heal the wound.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hematoma is descending within the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and press it with pincers; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hematoma is pressed, wash the eye with salty water, and cure the place of that which causes infection until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is woven into the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and severely to themselves, and they get the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to them; and because of this they lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their papers are underneath their eyelids, moistened by the inflammation and appearance covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the eye with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.

des poilz des papieres	And if a cold abscess comes to the area, apply a hot poultice until it is warm; then apply warm oil, and treat it with bandages.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz. Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if for someone who needs it, put a great quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make the entire bandage along the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large wound up to the small; and let one of the slits be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the heart, then scrape it all; then bring the two lips together with a stitch using a fine woolen thread and an awl, and remove any blood, and dry up the excess thread on the two edges with any sticky substance if you see fit to do so; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches using drying and constricting substances, because the paper lifts up at the wound's soudure [sealing] and its binding together, but the stitch is painful (as the ancients say), and this is a job without fear; and there is another way: it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is just like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three fingers separated according to the shape that is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out what is above with small scissors evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	If you cannot hold the tongs, and the object is not aligned, then take a needle and thread, and pierce it through the center of the wound; and take another thread and pass it through the large lip, and the second thread through the small one, and bring the threads together equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above which you have marked, as we have described; then bring the two lips of the wound together by sewing, and heal it until it is cured; and if an abscess forms at your incision, then calm it with cerulean and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hairs of the paper are converted: so you should use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of warts is as follows: convert the parchment and insert it according to what I have said, then make two warts by skill, and two fine threads as long as the width of the sputum and the broad part; then tie two threads at both ends where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other skillfully above what is on top of the parchment of the eye, and strain the two warts from the two formed parts; and leave it thus for several days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrivel up and fall off when it dries.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, and the wound has strength, then heal it until it is cured; and when the wound is sewed up, and if the paper is lifted, and the hairs no longer hurt; and this is the form of the two channels that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is such that you prick with a fine needle, and thread it with a fine and soft silk thread; then assemble the threads and tie them skillfully, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then prepare in the case a fine silk thread, and tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head into your hand; and let it be in the sun so that the work is declared, for it is a subtle and minute work, then pierce the needle all the way through the parchment to the root of the hair, and draw it out through the parchment until it comes out with the natural hair; then thread the hair into the case, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out through the case with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then treat the wound underneath all the way to the root that you have assigned to it, until the wound comes out from above the opening and you see it through the eye; then treat the wound and the thread, and close the eye and let it be closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, then accompany one long hair of the horse's tail, and let it grow with that one you leave it, until it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eye's pus
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "alacratia" or warts, comes into the eye, there are two ways in which it occurs: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting or cauterization, and by similar means.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is to split the growth, and loosen its lips, and place within it tents of linen, and keep it clean; and one must not use in its treatment anything that dries and constricts.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but one should work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or alder water, and linseed are cooked, and diaquilon ointment melted in some of the oils, and enveloped in a tent, and cured in this way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you must take care that it does not heal according to its former shape; and these works which we have said are not remedies for this disease, but preventions so that it does not return to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is beneath what is truly called "the brain", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; the way to treat them is for you to take a needle with a double thread, and pierce it into the flesh, and pass it through from one earlobe to the other, so that the thread runs through both ears; then the flesh above is closed up all around the needle, and the wound is wide open.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the wound returns as it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and insert it into the wound, and turn the wound inside out, and make two cuts along the sides within the wound; and let the edges of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you made, forming angles so that when they are stitched together, the shape is like that of the letter "Y" in the German alphabet; then remove this flesh, according to how much is hanging down below, from what follows the wound, then bring the two torn parts together and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we said before with softening medicines and bandages, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from a split or a stitch or cautery, then one should make a plain slit underneath the hair of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unsheathe between the two lips of the tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare remedies with all their might, so that they may bring the figure back to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is needed in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness happens to the scalp in such a way that the scalp above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then one should insert the tip of a razor underneath the scalp, and lift it upward; and press it with tweezers, until you grab what is cut into the spatulum, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot bear the pain of the too-sharp spatulum cutting into the eye; and your incision, by which you peel back this membrane, should be light, so that the scalp returns to its natural shape; and all of this assembly is healed, and they sometimes produce a saline solution in the eye, and raise it with sweet water, and use a bandage; then place a tent made of linen between the scalp and the eye, and place soft wool soaked in egg yolk on top of the eye; and after the third day, use the ointment and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles a hard cyst, and another which is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture; when touched by iron and pinched with tweezers, neither can be removed. Both appearances begin at the large tear duct, growing little by little until they cover the entire eye and its sight and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient tilts his head toward you, then he opens his eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then grab the nail with tweezers and pull it up slightly; then take a needle and thread through a horse, cow or ox hair, and double the end of the needle over, then pierce the nail with the entire needle, and tie the nail with a string and tie it above, then scrape all along the side of the nail where the tear duct is, up to the eyebrow, leaving the natural skin around the tear duct, so that by the incision the tears do not come out as usual; sometimes the nail is just stuck on the needle and thread, as we have said; then scrape it off all along the tear duct gently and with small movements.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the tear duct does not touch the thread and break it, and that the eyelid is not pierced; after the incision, put a little powdered chalk in the eye, and make a collar of litargir, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved and you cannot push in the needle and the hook cannot enter, this kind of nail is often cured by medicines; they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the disease, and take the spatulum gently punctured according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And draw the nail gently, and if you see that it is not lessened and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litarge and red copper and powdered chalk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same action, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts the eye greatly, then suspend it on the hook, and cut off a part but not all so that the body of tears does not come in; then distill into the eye red collar made from litarge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men, a red pustule sometimes emerges from the eye, covering the eyelid and pressing against the eyeball; it resembles a rose on a column. The patient should first place his head down, then open his eye, and press the pustule gently with his fingernail until all the pus is expressed; he should then hold it firmly in place. Next, cut the pustule's top and carefully scrape away all the pus, being careful not to injure the eyeball during this process. Make an incision as described earlier for the nail, using a small blade to remove any remaining matter; follow the instructions in this chapter for such incisions. Once the incision is complete and all the pus expressed, apply the yolk of a hard-boiled egg or red vitriol and similar corrosive medicines to the eye; place cotton soaked in egg white over the eye to protect it from heat. If anything remains, and the heat persists, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with cooling remedies. Then return to treating the eye until it is healed, and repeat this process for any other pustules that form in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should also know how to treat weak eyes by the natural way, and with surgery for accidental injuries; and do not insert your fingers in any of these procedures until you see that this member is suffering from that procedure.
des voines des eulz	of veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red lines that cover the eye, they hinder vision and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that you first examine the eye to see if there are any other diseases besides the veiny appearance; then proceed in this manner: instruct the patient to tilt their head back, then gently squeeze the veins all around the socket according to your expertise, making the incisions on the eyelid thin and double according to this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two edges be gradual in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then treat the veins firmly, and draw out the blood drop by drop after another, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to bruise the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not touch the veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to pull out all of them in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and there is assurance of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor should also examine the 'arissati' fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicine that burns according to what I have said before, if it is not healed, then there must be a cut made over the abscess where it should remain, and all the moisture within must be drawn out until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then it is necessary to use this instrument; and it is called an 'aspre chief', and it must be made from a very hard substance, with one end pointed like a file as shown in the present figure.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little while until you know that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the site with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the eyelids are glued together and no pus comes out, and the flesh of the eyelid is glued and remains that way for 40 days without any improvement or abscess forming, and no evil occurs, then you may be sure it is healed; but if not, there is another method to open the fistula at the edge of the eye socket according to this form: and it is necessary to expose the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is exposed, take out the forest according to this shape, and let the head of the tool be three-pronged, and the shaft be tapered to a point as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then he places it on the bone there, and moves his hand away from the eye a little, then returns to press down hard with the drill until it penetrates the bone, and the patient feels it through the windpipe if he keeps his hand over his nose; then he applies dry medicine as I taught you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened, he examines the matter in the nose; this is lighter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the output of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open all around and do not disturb the nose or cause thinning, then you should ligate the patient; then cleanse the eye, then place leeches or suckers without piercing to draw out fluid; then apply a poultice made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla onto the eye; then tightly bind the eye with bandages and linen; the method for the linen is that you take quite soft linen, double each piece in four, then place one on top of the other according to how much the eye needs; then tightly bind it from above with a sturdy bandage, and repeat the leeches without piercing to draw out fluid; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the ligature becomes loose, you should re-bind it tightly; then remove the ligature after one day and one night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then repeat the poultice, bandages, ligature, and leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear occurs in woven fabric, it opens and reveals something like a grain of resin, which is frightening to see; therefore, if you see it covering, the work is such that you thread a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then thread another needle with a double thread through the part of the tear; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the area of the double thread and tie one part of the fabric tightly, then pull out the needle and place wet woolen cloth on the eye; and leave it until the threads tear with the fabric, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is constrained by the fabric on each side in a circle of cloth, until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce them with a thin spatulum which comes from the bottom of the eye, and scrape away the white moisture and bring the eyes down, and enter in immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the corner of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but an abscess in the eye, resembling a descending inflammation, but it is not water; and the way to examine it is to make the patient sit upright on a chair, then take his head in your hands and move it until you see the abscess appear above your eyes; then let it be pierced, and the light blocked, and the patient should see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is an abscess, and if the discharge from the abscess is not clear as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	if you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatulum and insert it under the horny membrane at the point where the conjunctiva continues with the horny membrane and the cornea, until the bowstring is loosed; and when it is drawn out, distill into the eye honey mixed with hot water or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have discussed the appearances of diseases in the division, and what should be done to pierce them; now act according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands away from sunlight, and press his healthy eye firmly shut; then hold the paper over his eye with your left hand if it is his left eye, or your right hand if it is his right; then take in your right hand, if it is his left eye, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if it is his right; then place the point of the instrument alongside the cornea through the thickness of a hair at the outer edge of the iris to the part where the tear duct emerges, and push the instrument called «almagda» gently but firmly, and turn your hand so that it pierces the cornea, and you will feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and the depth of the path of almagda should be equal to the thickness of a hair from the edge of the pupil to the end of the iris; this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in the paper through the transparency of the horny membrane, and then push the instrument up into the space below one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he sees the water now, let the patient see it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the water rises again by the second way, put it down with the instrument; and when it is stuck in and does not rise, then gently draw out the almagda while turning your hand a little; and then put in the eye some little of the gem-water, and take away the instrument.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force into the eye cotton wool or linen moistened in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and bind it with clean cloth.Si li aigue ne vout point remonier, si leve la fuer de dedans la vierne et de l’oil avec un picquet de fer ou d’oile de paume et legierement avec un puitier de fer; puis li lie avec l’oil sain.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	If the water does not want to rise again, then lift the force from within the vein and eye with an iron rod or palm oil and gently with an iron spoon; then bind it with clean cloth. We, and those who are of our time, put on ground cumin mixed with an abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if  'almagda' cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  'alberit', which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And thus pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep, but make the incision subtle, then plug it with alum, as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep, causing him to lie on his back in a dark place; and he should be free of all movements, and take light food, and not move his head or to the right or left, and he should be bound according to his condition for three days; then release him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and show him some things, and then remove the bandage by the seventh day; and you should not do this during the hour of the operation or after the incision now, but you should alleviate it, so that the water rises gently.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And if there are abscesses in both eyes, you should release the bandage before the seventh day, and use the remedy for abscesses; and when it is healed, remove the sight-covering and put an eye-patch over one eye to cover it, and he should remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house a little at a time, and return to your bed; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they pierce and put almond milk into it, so that water is drawn out, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.Et s’il vient a l’oil que le tenebros ne peut estre remedeiz par nullis de cestz chapitrez, que tu deslie la veue et la metes en son leu, car il ne se pourait mie remedeer.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almagest , because those who do not know them will see them; and they are properly of iron:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of the needles have this same subtlety, and the hindmost are pointed in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or born children with various deformities, and some look like scorpions with many feet; and others have an encrusted discoloration of the skin, and others have a discolored discoloration.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those with the discoloration that is not encrusted, you should make the patient sit in your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils and pour the oil onto those spots, and pull them out hard; then use as much as you can bear of the subtle spear point, until you know that the discoloration is all gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing which we cannot cover, then open it at all .i. of the subtle instruments slightly, so that nothing remains; and if without you are overwhelmed, or abscess bad, then dry it as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is stained and all the flesh is removed, then pour or neat's milk and water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostrils open and moisture comes to the palate, you know it is healthy; and if moisture does not pass through as it should, you know there is a discoloration in the bone that blocks the instrument from cutting: therefore you must insert a thick linen thread through one nostril, and tie a knot with clean hands, and have between each knot as much space as a finger or less; then put the patient's head to the thread in their hand at their best strength, and pull it through the odorant until it comes out of the nose through the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull them apart gently while holding the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the teeth have corrupted the meat, then draw out the thread, wipe off the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the meat; and then put a plug of plaster in the nose for some days until it heals, and if it needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, through which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and it should have a handle to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid. And if you wish, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be hollow to clean out the ear; and have a plug in the ear to hold it while heating the oil or other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the tip of the nose; it grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye. Therefore, you should cut it at the beginning and remove all the pus; then apply fire cautery or burning medicine. If you delay cutting it until it becomes large, take care that it is not hard, of dark color, or insensate: do not touch it with iron, for this is a deep abscess. For when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient. If the abscess is due to touch and not to dark color, and you see that it can be entirely covered, then empty the wound and cut it without fear, cleansing the area of dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these upper cartilage, it benefits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then attach the two lips with a stitch, and cure it until it heals; and if the lips are torn on both sides, then you should scrape all the parts of their core until they heal, then sew up the two lips, and tie them, and powder dragon's blood and incense ground; and place a piece of strong plaster or other healing plaster over the powders, and leave it to heal by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you prepare the thread: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with a thread, as I have already informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, there are hard abscesses inside the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; therefore, you must twist the lips, and slit them at each end, then grab them with tweezers and cut into each part; then apply vitriated quicklime to the incision until the blood is stanched; and then leave it with garlic, and treat the area with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus"; you should hold it with tweezers, and cut at its root, and let the blood or pus run out; then apply powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, over the site. If the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again, and cauterize it; if it does not return after the cautery, that is how you treat an abscess.
des sordens	from filth
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are growths at the base of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, which are unsightly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, due to corruption in the gums, and they smell bad; you should make the patient hold his jaw open and expose the teeth or gums, removing everything until it is clean; and thus you should treat blackness, yellowness, greenness, and other discoloration, until they are cleaned. If what was removed at first returns, it is good; if not, then do it again the next day and the day after, until everything is removed. Know that teeth require various types of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the job shows you, so that the instruments used to clean between the teeth have different forms from those used to clean the gums; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a toothache that you delay pulling the tooth only as long as you can, because it should not be done; for it is a very serious matter to pull a tooth without cause.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain of the tooth socket.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient and he believes it to be in the healthy tooth socket; and he pulls out a good tooth and, despite this, the pain does not cease because the evil tooth socket remains, for we have already attempted this with these patients. And when you are certain of the tooth socket, you must then scrape around the tooth all the way to the gum; then move it with your fingers or with fine tweezers a little bit at a time until it is well loosened; then hold it firmly in the tweezers. Let the patient's head be between your knees and held steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of those instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you must fill it with lint, where the holes are; and gently clamp it with tweezers so that it does not break while being clamped; and one must work very gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it behind, and cause greater pain to the patient through the maliciousness of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of doing as unskilled surgeons do, who in their haste and audacity sometimes break the tooth, and do not listen to what we have told them; but sometimes they bring on great illness through the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine or garlic and vinegar; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply crushed vitriol to the site; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which make the teeth loose first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and they should be toothed to grip the roots.
de la racine des dens	of the tooth roots
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place, you should apply wet cotton wrapped in butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the area is soft. Then insert the forceps called "algefri," which make the shoulder look like a sick bird's beak; and inside, they are shaped like a file, and that is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is, a spatula, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through it, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, whose shapes come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one can also use this instrument with .ij. fingers, whose shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are in front of the reason for the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Let this instrument be so strong that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise, subtle master finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are many illnesses where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the variety of causes. And if it does not break in the bone or in any of the other bones, but protrudes, then he searches for the instruments that he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, by which these are the forms:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with suitable medicines. And if there is a protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When a tooth appears not according to nature, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be filed or ground down. Then pull it out; and if there is an air pocket with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron with a pointed end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And tap it gently day by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent that it can be ground down, then grind it with a file like this, in the shape shown:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the lime that needles are made from; and with lime gently prick the tooth little by little day after day, so that it does not move until it falls out; then smooth it completely at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loose, whether from blowing or hitting, and the patient cannot chew without defecating, and you have tried to treat it with constricting medicines but it does not work; then you must restrain them with a gold wire because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never moves. The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. If you see the teeth are moving, take the wire and wrap it twice around the two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth between the teeth, whether there is one or more, until blood comes from the healthy tooth on the other side. Then begin covering again up to the point where you started, and gently pull your hand while it is bleeding, so that it does not move. The ligature should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
