Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cover the head of the tooth with floss and grip it with tweezers, and bring them together, and hold them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not bite the tongue; then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone, or the floss breaks, then hold it with another piece of floss; let it remain and serve in this way for all time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of both healthy and diseased teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if one is put in its place, fresh after fresh, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should attempt this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from a cow's bone, and it is put in the place where there is a defect, and it is restrained as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	cut off the hair of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes under the tongue is born like that; or it can be caused by an accident or wound; and the treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, and press his head against your healthy one, and hold his tongue; then grasp the thick nervous ligament with tweezers, as wide as the tongue is dislocated from its socket, and if there is hardness or swelling, it is due to a sudden wound, so it should be pricked with an awl and grasped with the tweezers; take care that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery underneath; when you have finished, lift the patient's head with rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then place a tent made of linen under the tongue; and tie the patient's tongue every night so that it cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply ground vitriol to the area; and if the blood clotted, cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this. Then treat it further until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is black or hard and the patient doesn't feel any pain, then don't touch it, as it is likely a cancerous growth. If it is declining towards a blister and there is moisture, pierce it with a needle and release the fluid with a gentle spatulum, opening it from both sides. If bleeding occurs due to your intervention, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until all the pus is drained. Raise the affected area with poultices of garlic and salt, and treat the wound with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are sores in the throat called "godath," and they are properly called almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if they are hard abscesses of a small size and a light color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent bleeding; but let it be until it is mature, and then you will burst it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is thin, have an instrument ready to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess is calm and pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with his chin in your hand and his mouth open, and the surgeon holds the instrument between his hands, and presses the tongue down below all the apparatus, from which comes its shape; it should be made of fine silver or brass, as thin as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then press the tongue down with the instrument and you will see the abscess. Take a pair of tweezers and grab it, pulling it out of the tonsil and up towards the surface as far as possible; pull some threads from the cloth along with it, then cover the instrument again, which should be shaped like a hook, to create a grip, and is made of either iron or copper.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument available, use tweezers, which should be shaped like a hook:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it has a sharp point on one end and a flat edge on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and with water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with water, or with peels of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two tonsils appear in the throat, so cut them thus as the two tonsils are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was deep in her throat; it was specifically a small, sensitive abscess. Her entire throat was swollen, so the woman couldn't breathe through the opening, which was blocked, nor eat or drink, and she would have died within one to two days had this continued.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had pushed up two warts from the back of her throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly went to work and inserted the probe into one of the openings in her nose, then pulled it taut, and cut out a large chunk of the abscess; I then repeated this process on the other nostril, and opened up her mouth, pressing down on her tongue. Next, I inserted the probe into the abscess, removing another portion, but only a little blood came out; this cleared the airway in her throat, and she could now drink water and wine, and we continued to cut away at the abscess for an extended period of time. The abscess would shrink, then grow again, filling up the space I had emptied, so I packed it with a poultice, and cauterized it from within the throat; this stopped its growth. I left those parts, and God did the rest after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the iris descends to the eyeball, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round beneath, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it has been cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pus is abated, and it is thin; and it is round and not long; and it is blood-red or a fuschia color or black, then you should avoid incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have described, of its whiteness and length, you should cause the patient to sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument of which we have made mention earlier; then insert the hook into the eye, and draw it beneath, and scrape with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almond-shaped areas.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover anything more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it hurts the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two testicles, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use an incision to treat his fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is for acute fever.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head on your lap, and then press his tongue against the instrument that we described in the chapter on cautery, and mix it with hot water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the application of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle on its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and you place the instrument with all the medicine on the pupil; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine run out of his mouth and do not go down into his throat and lungs. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the pupil for the duration of half an hour, until you see it become numb and the bites of the medicine are pacified. And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton on top, so that the cotton sticks to the pupil; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and remove it after four or five days. And if you need to renew the cautery with medicine, then renew it, and after the cautery, wash around the pupil with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and use a cold compress, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery. If it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, wormwood, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and in the pot there is one instrument with a handle shaped thus:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one of the ends should be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapors rise into the eye through the canal until the eye is deadened; then repeat this often, until the eye dries out, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because many things can happen there; nor do this after the hot abscess has broken.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not available, take a stick and place an egg white on the tip so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; because the egg white will not allow the vapors to trouble the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fish spine, or some object, gets stuck in the throat; so you must try to remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with the whole instrument, so that you can move the object; and if it does not come out and is lodged in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the spot, it will lodge there, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have described, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and let the head be raised upward; and beware of touching the epiglottis, lest it be torn, nor push the bone in; and move the patient's head so that he vomits, in order to dislodge the object; then he swallows the instrument, so that he can dislodge the object; if he cannot swallow it, then pull it out with the whole instrument, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the remedy is to bleed the patient, as I have said in the section on remedies; and if this does not help, then examine the throat of the ill person towards the sun, and then press their tongue with the instrument I have described to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a pointed stick, and insert it into the throat of the ill person; then heat the tip of the stick with hot iron, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, moving it around with his hand frequently; and as soon as he feels the water, he will spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not work as we have said, then suffocate the patient with assafetida smoke, using the instrument I described for smoking out the uvula; do this several times, because it will work without bleeding.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of the smoking is that you put hot charcoal in a pot, and cover it with a perforated lid, and in the hole put the end of the instrument; then pour your smoke into it, and the patient puts his head back in his mouth, closing his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes to the uvula; and the uvula will come out now, and if it does not, repeat the smoking several times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salted and sour things, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for him to go out because of this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to pull the saliva is, when you can see it, similar to curved tweezers that can enter the throat; it should be shaped like a surgeon's forceps, with roughness from lime so that it can grasp and not let go; here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, as the recollections that come after one and another in this book show, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two kinds, one in its appearance itself, and in what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is due to the locations where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundations, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And with abscesses one must not pierce until the bowels are dead according to their completion; and there are some that one must pierce when they become crusty, and they do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets it be so long that it is pus around, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.Et si il le percierent, et il se curast adés, si est cause de grant mal a celui qui a la jointure, car il ne puet remuer li meisme membre tant qu’il vult.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay piercing it until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; where it is near the fundament, one must pierce it so that it may be cured; and one must not pierce an abscess without digestion being complete, except for one that is near the fundament, lest it burst inside and become elongated, and a fistula ensues, taking a long time to heal.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time of piercing an abscess that is mature according to its digestion, and it is when the pain has subsided, and the decrease in fever, and the lessening of swelling and redness, and the improvement in appetite and the appearance of pus; and one must pierce where the abscess is most dependent, and where there are signs of pus forming. And the piercing should be at a distance from the heart, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no folding of the skin.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	For those who bend, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the piercing wait until it is confirmed with digestion complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it too soon, the body's venom will flow along with it, and it will be filled with filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess which has been pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses with large incisions, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that one should chew the skin, and cover; when it has become as soft as a drape, and is deadened, then one must do the same as for blisters: and if there are some that are split into three angles, and some which one covers just like the fruit of the myrtle; and if there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those which have no head, like a superficial abscess, one must pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large, and has collected a lot of pus, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but some part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again from it; do this several times from time to time, until all the pus comes out; likewise if the patient is very weak, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes an experienced surgeon jumps with the release of gas from the belly, which may kill the patient, and you would not know it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, cleanse the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, apply a tent made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then insert a tent in each one so that they press against each other; and if you have slit the skin around the abscess and pulled it open, then fill it with old cotton or dried linen rags without moisture, and tie it up for three days; then remove it and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and vinegar, and moisten the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and healing, and use the powders I have described in this book with your hands; and if it is winter, and the area around the abscess is very nervous, place wet tents and clothes drenched in warm wine and oil over it; but if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, place wet clothes drenched in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, over it for a third of a day, as we have said; then cut into the abscess, wash and clean it, and treat it as needed until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And so it is necessary to understand generally in the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how one must go about treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the neck come small abscesses, which are common in people who work in wool, like the pimples on a goat's udder; there are many variations of these.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and others where there is moisture as well as pulsation; and there are some that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause a contrary effect.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the waist are such that you should test all instruments called "dislocators", from which the forms come later, what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will push it out from above the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, they will scorch it without leaving anything behind that contains the moisture, for it will return again if nothing is left; then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment, if present; otherwise, in water and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will recover.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know it will not stay during the night; then treat the wound with ointment that is appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus, treat it as follows: cut it according to this form from the long side; and pour out your fingernails, and scrape off all of it, and put all of your treatment on drawing out the pus beneath the skin where it lies; and if the artery makes a noise against you, do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat an abscess if it is piercing, and cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut on the piercing abscess and moistness is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses have no moisture in them, and these were the abscesses that I opened in a woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if someone had cut into them, they would have caused just as much bleeding as if they had cut into a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses coming from the head, or those that come from the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should be left uncovered for as long a time as possible, so that pus can issue out; and treat it as it should be treated.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin area, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and some are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located within its own section, as are the nodule and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities among these scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are stubborn and do not want to heal.And li chiés des enfans si adont qu’il ont scrophule dedens le col, ou dedens la teste, ou dedens les oreilles, ou dedens les costes, et il n’i a pas de scrophule qui ne contienent moistor et sanguine.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Here then, when you see one that is of good disposition for cauterization, and is similar in color to the body, and quiet in every part, and not swollen at the nerves of the neck or artery or duct, and not deep; then you should cover it from above, and cut away at each part, and have the two lips of the heart at an angle, if you need them, as we have said for abscesses of the head. And draw it a little at a time, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and do not use a spatula or knife too much, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, but only cover what you need to.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, then put into the wound vitriol crushed, or any powders that stop bleeding, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess is pacified, and the wound softens, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is healed, return to your work, so that you may complete it; then examine with your finger if any small scabs remain, and pick them off and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, you should not pick that scab, but ligature it with a strong double thread, and let it fall without causing harm; then treat the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you pick the entire scab, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that no superfluity remains due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should attend to picking at its root, and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulae that hold superfluity, pierce there where it appears to be dying; and pierce in the same way as aforementioned, hanging down, then administer tenting with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remaining of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then cure with ointment smeared on a piece of cloth, until it heals.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of cutting the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the written account of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with scrofula, it is necessary to cut the throat, which is called the "epiglottis"; and one should not make an incision through this, because all the veins and the lungs are affected by the disease in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lungs, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it under the three or four circles, with a small slit across, between the two circles, or according to the amount of the slit in the hyoid bone; and those places that are susceptible to the splitting of the epiglottis, there should be no flesh, and the vessels should be long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat to the very edge, then split the cartilage until he reaches the hyoid bone; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the hyoid bone, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the flow of blood from the hyoid bone that is broken, and by the defect in the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and heal it all along without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote healing, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely healed, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then they cut open the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe through the wound and thus be kept from dying; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it passes in three or four days. Then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took a knife and stabbed herself in the throat, cutting through some of the windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood had not come out through the throat or windpipe but instead was escaping through the wound itself.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it healed; and the maiden had no more trouble with her voice, and recovered fully; therefore I say that one should not be afraid to cut into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large hernia in color like jaundice, and it is much found in women; and it has two manners: natural and accidental; or the natural kind has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is according to two manners: one is similar to a hernia like a tumor, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear of it, and one should not operate by force except in the one that is small, and test and probe all the entrance: if you find it as soft as a tumor, and cannot be forced at all, cut it as one cuts a tumor, and pull it out to its root, if there is no way to heal it; and probe thoroughly, and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many methods available, all of which I will describe in detail; but now I must explain the difference between a cut and a dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is hot and feverish, as long as the boil has not passed, and the pus is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a cut there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body; it starts like a boil and becomes large; they are according to their appearances, either dry, moist, or both, and according to their color as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and examine it with an instrument called an "introducer", according to what its shape comes from in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of probing abscesses is to squeeze in the most moist place you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers slightly, until you feel that the pus has been discharged according to the size of the abscess; then extract the probe, and take care not to push it in too far.Et s’il avient que li estrumens soit si dur qu’il ne porrat pas aler si loins ou il fust necessaire, mets li estrumens sus li pomer et li col de l’aposteme, et par le fort de la force, leve li deuxis et tire li col a toi; et si tu vees que li col soit si dur qu’il ne porrat pas aler si loins ou il fust necessaire, mets li estrumens sus li pomer et li col de l’aposteme, and by the strength of your force, lift the two sides and pull the neck towards you; and if you see that the neck is so hard that it cannot go as far as necessary, place the probe on the head and the collar of the abscess, and with a strong effort, lift the two sides and pull the neck towards you.Et s’il avient que li col soit si dur qu’il ne porrat pas aler si loins ou il fust necessaire, mets li estrumens sus li pomer et li col de l’aposteme, et par le fort de la force, leve li deuxis et tire li col a toi; and if you see that the neck is so hard that it cannot go as far as necessary, place the probe on the head and the collar of the abscess, and with a strong effort, lift the two sides and pull the neck towards you.S’il avient que l’aposteme soit en la fesse, ou il ne porrat pas aler si loins ou il fust necessaire, mets li estrumens sus li pomer et li col de l’aposteme, and with a strong effort, lift the two sides and pull the neck towards you.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus runs freely, no matter what color it is, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if no pus comes out after the incision, know that it is a fatty abscess, so treat it in the form of a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side and examine the skin where it lies, to draw it out healthy with your nail; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing is left in it, it will return many times; and if a little remains and the wound does not trouble you, employ some corrosive powders on the wound, and tighten the wound, and apply healing abscess remedies until it is healed; and if the wound is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what creates scabs.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein pulsating is contrary or other, you hurry and apply powdered vitriol to the spot, and leave it for 2 days or 3, until the wound suppurates, and the blood flow subsides; then return to cover what has remained of the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the instruments for probing, and they come in three varieties: large, medium, and small. There are also three types of probes called "albaret", one type is called "breb", and there are three varieties of these: large, medium, and small, to probe abscesses and fistulas. They are similar to the needles used for sewing up wounds, made from brass, iron, or silver. The yellow-colored ones are more effective for probing fistula cavities, and they are also available in black steel, best suited for probing fistula cavities. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the probes vary greatly, as you can see: large, medium, and small. There are also probes with two curves that come in three varieties, and probes with three curves which are also available in three sizes. Probes with a single curve come in two varieties, and all these types are essential for different purposes.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these, with which one cuts, are sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, which are used to scorch the nose, so that one does not cut the vein or nerve; and with such introducers, bleeding is stopped in wounds, so that the patient does not bleed to death when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are not used except in fleshy places, like legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes a small instrument is made, resembling a slice of a clove, according to this form, with which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the place that heals by filling the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are filled according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to become corrupt, so that they look like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and if one wants to cure them, one should bleed them according to this form from this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scorch the fat, and fill the wound with medicine, then sew up the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sags down, and is softened due to its size as happens to women, then make two cuts above, through similar incisions; so that one is attached to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from line .b. up to line .g.; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you should fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it dissolves the remaining skin and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula and they have nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who retain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the content of the abscess is drained, then fill the wound with clean cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and dress it with suitable ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like scrofula, then treat them as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is closed, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is open and the skin above it, this often causes abscesses; and so does the swollen vein and abscess. And so one recognizes that it is from an artery when the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tugging; and when it is from a vein, there are discolored spots appearing; and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits or in the groin or neck or many other places, and they are large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one must avoid cauterizing with iron, and also avoid cauterizing the head, and on that which is swollen from an artery, make an incision above the skin that the long artery is under; then cut away neatly along the edges, and separate the artery from the veins, so that it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath one of the edges, and pierce it through to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, according to how I instructed you in the extraction of the two temples; then pierce the area between the two threads with an instrument, so that the blood that is inside flows out, and releases the abscess; then administer treatment with warm bowels, until the thread relaxes; then treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is from a vein incision, you should dye your hand with something from the abscess all over the skin, then insert a needle underneath the area that you are holding in your hand, and pierce it through, and have a double thread there, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you at either end of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will come out, insert another needle under the entire thread throughout the abscess at the incision site of the first needle, and bind the thread in three places; then cut the abscess so that the excess flows out, then cut the excess from the skin and leave what is tied; then place a moistened cloth with wine and oil on top, and administer treatments with poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, they also come in the nerves when they are injured, or from too great exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and everywhere there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain; and when one presses it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body but under the skin; and it is mute throughout, and cannot move forward or backward, or down or up, and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron: for there could be contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, treat with a poultice.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root; and if it is large, slit it with a knife, and scrape it, then cut out the pus and stitch up the wound to be healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large, hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At times it occurs in the abdomen and nowhere else; it is a disease called "mushroom" due to its resemblance to mushrooms, with thin roots and thick branches. There are small ones and very large ones. I saw a man who had two of them on his abdomen that looked more like mushrooms than anything else, without any difference between them; they were white, had slender roots, and had split open, from which moisture flowed.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found that one weighed 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces. The treatment for this is to make an incision and see if the disease is moist; the color of the wart should be white and moist with thin roots. Then cut it with a spatulum, making it wide, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in surgery there are often excessive bleeding, and if the blood flows, then you must hurry to cauterize it; and if you see that the patient is terrified and fearful of the incision with the iron, then take a well-made thread, and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it cuts the joint, and cuts it without any effort; and if the roots are thick, then be fearful of cutting them too, especially in the abdomen, but you can cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not grow back; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the skin which is a pale color and has poor sensation and a milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is a deep abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure of an ulcer, and it is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as happens in other routs, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind; and if it is from the rout of the ulcer and from the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a minor thing without pain, and opens through diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it pops out, and then returns in, and sometimes it is dried up, and increases a lot at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue and will open easily when you press it with your hand, without any constraint; and if it is due to blood, the abscess will be large and hard, and will have a fixed amount of pus in it; and if it is due to wind, there will be swelling on the touch, and the treatment should consider whether the appearance is from arterial blood or venous blood, or from wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you are to leave the wound untreated, then:
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding both the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowel, then instruct the patient to tighten his armpit and hold it straight, then sign around the wound all around; then have him lie down between your hands, and move around the area that you marked for the spasm, then press down on half of the abscess towards the nail, and tie it tightly with a strong thread or silk cord; then operate on the other half of the abscess above the ligature, and probe the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligature, release it and probe the intestine out of the abdomen; and if you find the bowel, grab it by the nail and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein is causing resistance, move away from it and return to your treatment, take two needles and insert two strong threads through them, then pierce around what you have made in a cross shape; then pull the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see anything, remove the needles and leave the wound to heal on its own; or scrape away the dead flesh when it becomes thin and healed, then treat the wound as needed and lance the abscess as we have described; then extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound appropriately and close it up.
dou chancre	for sores
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the types of sores and how to treat them with medicine, including cauterization with iron; now we shall speak of sores appearing in the throat, and great care is needed in their treatment. Ancient scholars say that when sores appear in places where they can be reached by scraping, such as on the nipples, thighs, or other similar areas, they should be completely removed at their onset. However, once they become large and chronic, one should not attempt to treat them, for I have never seen anyone healed from such sores, nor has anyone ever been healed from them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you sometimes purge the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has manifest fullness; then prepare the site for the operation; then shave the area around the ulcer and the head of the wound, and the bone all around without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and squeeze well the site with your hand or something, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein makes you feel uncomfortable, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
