If not, make him breathe through ventouse cups on his back and nipples without bleeding them; then take a blanket, soak it in juice of plantain or dogwood with old wine, and have him breathe over the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has drained, treat the wound with ointment until it heals; and if it is called 'albathir', which is red and looks like rough ash, cover it as I said before; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Here is the translation of the text into English:
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses arise in the body, such as sores and pus-filled abscesses and herpes and boil and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have described in the classification.Et li apotomes de fevre sont plusors: or l’un est de la fleme; or l’autre est de sang; or l’autre est de sang et de fleme.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess that occurs in the bowels, which is not among the abscesses that are found in the body; and if you wish to know the nature of iron, observe whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and whether it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So do not be in a hurry to pierce it, but let it drain as long as the pain is relieved; and then let the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats for him to lean on, and support his back and rest his feet against something firm; and let his buttocks be spread out, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then suck the orifice towards the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the orifice of the abscess, through which the pus comes out later; and it is necessary that when you administer this instrument, you insert the rod first to determine the depth of the abscess, so that what goes into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the abscess with fabric so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; and let him hold the nozzle of the instrument up, and tighten the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and they make it in the soft hand, then it must be covered with a bandage at the head, with a light sponge; and when the bowels are evacuated, then you should put into the wound moist tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the tent out of the wound at the bottom of the wound, and put a poultice over the wound and over the wound a clean linen cloth moistened in water or malva leaves that have been cooked; then cure after two days of ointment, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the wound and the wound by an enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and aristolochia that have been cooked for a long time; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the wound, then you should guard against cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the natural shape of childbirth, and the signs that it is time when you see the woman pushing downward, and wanting to smell the air; then hasten the child to come out; then you know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the afterbirth comes out with the child, and the mother's superfluities are cleaned away through good purification; and one who comes in a different way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out feet first, or head or shoulder first, or by the arms; it may come out upside down, or in other bad positions; so the midwife must be wise and cunning in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the different ways to assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby is born head-first in a natural delivery, and the woman is struggling, and her vitality is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be supported by other women; prepare an aromatic oil made from cooked celery seed or fenugreek, and then use a small spatula to apply it between her buttocks, as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the membrane, and press on her nail until the moisture that is within flows out; and press the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then the woman must be clistened with a poultice of fenugreek and olive oil; then have her press and sneeze with incense, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now let the child come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, then you must gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up; then stand the chair on the ground, and hold one the woman so that she does not strain while standing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then grab the hands at the nail which was mentioned before, and pull out the child, and reset in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out of its feet, it should be pushed upward; and then rock it back and forth gently until it is even; then grab one foot and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he jumps up to his ankles, instruct him to grab hold and make him sneeze from the back; if he jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump out as we have said, then pull it back and forth gently until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he doesn't come out as we have described, take myrrh, and olive oil, and gum, and grind them all in a mortar; and put some of this ointment inside the woman's birth canal, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is soft down there, make her wear a collar of myrrh around her neck, and keep it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and gently squeeze her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child will come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, put your hands on his head little by little; then lie him down on his stomach, with his feet hanging down, and let him lie on his back; and bend his arms little by little, and then press his hands on his belly, and lift up his buttocks from below, until he is aligned downward; and if the child does not cry out, take his feet and move them around, then move his belly upward, then put your hands in; and rock the child little by little; and command the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's exit, which comes out as wide as a hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I want to try to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed and lift her legs up straight; then apply the mustard poultice that I described; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then work on bringing the hand back; and rock the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the baby's exit on its neck, and have her hands spread out, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the midwife to dye her hand, then gradually turn it, and move it gently; and when it is even, she should apply a poultice of mustard and oil, as we have said, then she must command her to move it gradually; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way all the afterbirth, then scrape away the afterbirth with your fingernail until the moisture is expelled; and if the child turns its face and neck, then scrape it from there, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then insert the child inside, as you have placed it where it should be, and command the woman to grip several times: then release it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange things and do not live, unless by name; I know that they are multiplied and separated by the stylet that divides them, which is bound to the udder; and sometimes they issue as naturally as a pig, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue profusely, then the surgeon should act as we have said, and be quick and skillful in his actions; and he should do whatever benefits the patient.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb as one, or two, or three, or four, or five, or six, or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all shaped like children according to the measurement of the glorious sage; and the surgeon should know this, for sometimes similar things happen to them; so act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child or distended womb, as I have said in the division, and there is no discharge, and you must use manual pressure; then you should know if the woman is of sound health and free from fear of death; then the woman should be supported on her back with her head declined downward and her legs raised; and the surgeon should use the ten fingers, or she should be tied to the bed so that she does not move when the child is delivered; then the surgeon should rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with myrrh, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then anoint his hands with these oils and myrrh; then he should enter them gently into the womb, then seek the place where the child is located so that it may descend onto its head; then he should insert the fingers at the sides, or under the chin, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or below the beard, or in the throat, or near the ribs; and if the delivery is from the feet, then he should insert them at the heel and the sides; and he should use the index finger of his right hand, and place the crook between his left thumb and forefinger, and enter it gently into the womb, and insert the finger in any of the places we have mentioned until it reaches the empty space; and this is how the finger should be shaped:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then file against the other nail, or the third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then they are filed evenly by moving from one side to the other, to move out, and the nails are bitten to hold, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remain, then anoint the nail of one of his fingers with oil and rub it in that part, and pull the other; and if nothing remains, then put the file or higher, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back due to the dislocation, then you must wrap a cloth around it until it pops out; then grab the joint of the wrist or the elbow, and thus you must do for the other hand and feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is tight in the birth canal, and it has a sharp pain gathered at its head, then you should push the spathumile [sponge] between your fingers, and press on the head and draw out the fluid; or you should pierce it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and likewise do if the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with tweezers, and if the head jumps out and is forced by the forceps, it should be split open so that the fluids in the birth canal come out; and if it cannot come out, pierce it in pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you should pierce it so that the fluids flow out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is above his feet, the pulse is light, and the breath comes easily to the mouth.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or the foot, you should pull it out with the cloth wrapped around his hand; and make an incision in the belly or the foot, so that the moisture that is there flows out; and if other members are stuck, and the bowels remain, he puts his hand into the wound up to the bottom of the wound; then he puts in a hook or two, and pulls it out; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has formed there, one should not work on it, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and the provider applies poultices, and uses warm and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the placenta is on his side, and you can make it even, then one should administer what we have said for a live child; and if one cannot do this, then pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it is administered to those with abscesses that come in the sea; and if there is a discharge of blood, let it be placed in warm water, and give other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose fetus had died within her; then another was sewn over him, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came in his arm, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to discharge profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought long and hard, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong drawing plaster, and out came a bone, and after a few days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I lanced the wound and extracted the bone, so that the woman was in a better state; and she lived for a long time like this, and sometimes a little pus would come out of the site; and I only mention this chapter because when the master finds a strange thing, he should know how to apply a remedy.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the dislocated shoulder to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, to which one adds the books; and at .2 turns as .2 heads of .2 lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horn should be more slender than the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the instrument should be two digits wide, and the edges of the wood should be one digit and a half long; and in both ends there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly attached at both ends, half a digit or a little more in length; and these two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the sea to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of tweezers; and has at its two ends two adjustments, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you see open the wound all over the instrument, then make the woman lie on her bed, her feet dangling and her legs open, then fit together the two adjustments in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then work your hand all over the instrument, as you did with tweezers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the wound, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated, and their appearances are multiplied; and when the patient sees them prepared, the action is faster and higher in people because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair over the instrument, but prepare it, for their need is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold in her breath, then make her sneeze with some scent, and pinch her nose and mouth; and if she vomits through that, all the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, one should take a container and make an opening in its lid, then place herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calendula, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are to be cooked in water over fire. Then place one end of a cane or pipe into the container and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and apply it so that the vapors enter the wound. Then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the pus comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not cured, one should instruct the midwife to wet her left hand with oil of sesame or with musk-moss, then place it into the natural opening and search for the placenta. When she finds it, she should grasp and stretch it gently bit by bit, so that the wound does not tear during extraction; but she must move it slightly from side to side and then pull it out. Then it will come out and be dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the wound is narrow, we have discussed the cure for sneezing and the fumigation of herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, beware of following the wrong path; but you should tie what is at the mouth of the wound to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with an ointment of tetrafarmaçon; then she will pass it and recover, and it will come out; but nevertheless, when she passes it, there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and the disease is made worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If necessary, suitable fumigations should be used for this: some ancient writers have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained placenta and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like glass in appearance, and its head is fine in nature, and its feet are wide on the fire; and there is fumigation over the charcoal, and the stain until it is wasted, and another one begins.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without the foreskin pierced, but with a subtle hymen; therefore, it is necessary that the midwife pierce this hymen with her finger and not with a sharp instrument, and she should keep the wound clean so that it does not touch it; then she should apply moist linen soaked in wine and oil, and then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, then put a wooden splint through the wound and leave it for several days, then remove it when the child wants to walk around.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes the healing comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it must be covered suddenly: then it should be treated, as we have said, with a wooden splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodules, and they grow larger than those that come from within the rectum, or in the space between the two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodule is old, it opens up, and usually white moisture or thin pus flows out, and sometimes these fistulas are bleeding. They are perceptible by the fact that the patient either expels gas or has a bowel movement when he makes an effort, and sometimes they discharge on their own.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulæ which penetrate as far as the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they can reach the joint of the thigh, and down to the testicles.Et si a fistules qu’advenent desoz le fondement et par les costes ou par la nuque, ou par le petis de la cuixe; et sont mals aincis.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula is bleeding or not; and it is when you push your finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle made of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twist in it.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has a twist, you insert a thin probe made of lead or a horsehair, as far as you can feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you cannot feel it, and there is no discharge or farting or pus coming from the opening, as we have said, then know that it has not yet broken through; so be quick about treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates as far as the bladder or the duct of urine, and urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, then the vein will flow as far as the site; if there is tortuosity and pain in the surrounding area, then it must be bound there, and ointments are useless; and for these bleeding fistulas, there is no cure beyond effort, and folly of those who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	For one that is not bleeding and is not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have experienced; and the patient lies on his back, and the leg is lifted up to the thigh, and the thigh bent towards the belly; then pierce a vein with an awl, or with lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the vein is coming from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must push your finger in there, if you feel that the vein has pierced through; and it should be uncovered where you feel a lump or swelling on the flesh, then you know that it is bleeding; do not work on it if one cannot heal it.Si li tentens sont tortuosez entor la char, et n’a point de dolor adés que soit grant, si convient qu’il soit remes en son leu par oignement qui contrient li membres; s’il ne peut demourer ains revient, si covient il que tu le bates tant qu’il soit contriet.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can still sometimes heal them, but this rarely happens; and the help one gives is to scorch the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and he fills it all with heat in the fistula, as far as it goes towards the anus; and do this two or three times, until you know that these false humors are burned, which look like a feather of a bird; and then cure with moist bandages, as long as these humors come out, and then cure with ointment, closing up the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not healed in this way, it cannot be otherwise; and if the tent goes inside and does not reach the rectum which is at the anus, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of humor or of syphilis, and you see the fistula below the covering towards the anus; then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and fill it in front of the tent, and then cauterize after it, as far as it comes to the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered, and will fall out; then remove those false humors which look like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus comes out and flows between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with an astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery draws together two things: that is, the scorching of the flesh around the wound, and the zastening of blood and drying of moisture; then the dressing of moist bandages with butter or crushed substances, until the swelling goes down and the burned flesh comes out; then treat the wound with quick-drying ointments on hard, dry flesh, and these are the dry remedies.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the foundation, and is removed from the body, put your finger or foundation in it, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between them is the membrane or flesh, or it is about to pierce, do not lose hope and expectation through the administration of one of three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut it deeply to the bottom; if you can, place bandages and treat as before; do not go too deep, lest you damage the underlying structure and cause the wound to discharge; then treat as already described; perhaps it will heal. Remove that covering and clean after cutting away from the bottom membrane, by tent or other sharp instrument; then cauterize the wounded flesh in the wound, as much as you can; then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula open on the outside of the structure: this is a lighter burden for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this way: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation below the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread into it, and he inserts the tent along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that opening, so that you put your finger on the foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and compress them together, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes compress it until the threads scrape against each other and heal; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open on its own, then you must make it open in every way that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover the wound with a bandage, then treat it, as we have said, until it has healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile thorny, which one makes for the fistula, is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other; and not sharp on the side that one does not want to scrape, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some discharge blood, and there may be one or more, and they are outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and yet they discharge a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the body; and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to strain himself to go to the toilet until the anus relaxes and the hairs become visible; then you hurry and grab it with tweezers, or hold it with your fingernail, then pull it out by its roots; and if the nails cannot hold it because of moisture, they are grabbed with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair; and they are pulled out with your fingers, then cut off, and powdered with some hot powder that is used for cauterization; or you cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, and then treat other ailments until he recovers; and if the anus cannot relax, you give the patient a strong, bitter enema to wash away what is inside the anus so that it can relax; when the patient strains, and the hairs come out of the anus, the treatment is easy; and you grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, then cut them off, and treat them as we have said until he recovers and fears incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must perform surgery in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it through a needle, and then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side; turn both ends of the thread below the needle and tie it tightly; then tie the thread, remove the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one to stop the flow of blood. Then place a moistened cloth in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and apply pressure on the wound, and command the patient to rest. Then let him lie down until he feels better; when he is healed, treat it with ointment and other remedies.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Drying of the bowels occurs often in the intestines, due to constipation from natural causes, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must cut a boil at the tip of a spatula or your finger, do not let it get moist; then treat it until it is dry as it should be. If it cannot heal, cut it again more forcefully than before, until it heals and the skin is peeled; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance formed under the body, and they move very quickly; sometimes the frost bites them, and one feels them as if dead from trembling, and they come throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather of an owl's feather, or a strong vulture's feather, and put that feather on the trembling, until the purple circle trembles all around it; then turn your hand over the entire feather, so as to scoop out the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, make a cane of bronze or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and drawn out on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	nor pierced, so that it may hold the finger, and press firmly. And if you see fit, cauterize the vein, just as it is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they are made of silver or brass, or melted copper or wire; and sometimes they are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which are administered for the treatment of children and the weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a division where the bellies are tied, as you see, and the intestines are pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is where one puts the medicines in a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is an inch of space between each hole, then thread a strong twisted thread through these holes in the shape of X or around, and gather the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then enema.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white, or similar, then insert it gently; then press the minister's hands together around it until it is all sucked in, then withdraw the syringe, and let the patient lie on his side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him cough as much as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterwards, it is even more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the clistere for the disease of stomach ache, and the medicine rushes to come out, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or an abscess, then let the syringe be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin syringe that pulls on the skin:
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will discuss the cures by hand and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by splitting of stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or that are made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the leg, or the belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then make him bleed with the cephalic itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and keep the patient from fullness of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then reduce his food intake and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put cotton soaked in rose oil only on the wound, or in astringent wine, if there is a hot abscess; and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound, if it has all its blood and has not been moved by air.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together with tenting, then stitch them together, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can be reached with a cupping glass; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as meat and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pus in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then scoop out all of the pus and let it flow out; then treat it with medicine. And if there is a vein or artery in the wound, which causes bleeding without stopping, and it cannot be staunched with medicines, then tie off the artery and, if that doesn't help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light; you should put on this powder which heals as soon as the burn is healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and powdered very finely, then apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place until it dries well and joins all its blood; and then bind it up well, and leave it without loosening, if it doesn't swell; for the medicine is not removed until the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with chalk alone, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound is moved by the fire.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, let it be in the same state, and do not put any of this powder on it; but apply some digestive ointments, or barley flour made with water and honey, until it is soft; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with subtle tweezers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is single, then there is no difference between it and one in the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but let the cure proceed, and put nothing constricting on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them withdraw; and put nothing cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be moist, as in the case of a wash made with honey and rose oil, and cooked with water, and other stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and bind it, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is a cavity and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower spot; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, then stop it, and ligature it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage for food is blocked, then cut the windpipe on the neck's Adam's apple, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then compress it gently, and leave it for several days, then cleanse the wound with poultices until it heals; and if the wound has affected the bone, then trepan it; and if there are bone fragments, then extract them all if you can, and those that you cannot reach, then leave them as they are until the wound granulates and is closed; and if the wound is fresh, then apply the powder I mentioned earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in that chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound bleeds when the wind blows on it: then you will know that the wound is deadly; but if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it because of the blood that seeps through, and returns to the body, and kills the patient; but put on an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and let the patient sleep with his head on the wound for three days or four, or more; then no spasms, nor bad tremors of the body, nor straining of the wind will come; and when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it therefore with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and there is a fistula, then treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether in front or behind, then treat it as one who is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, powder it, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has torn pieces, then clean the wound, and draw out the foreign bodies if they are embedded; and for other wounds in other parts, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Ruptures of the belly occur in great, medium, and small sizes; from a large wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines may protrude, causing the entrance of air; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, because one must stitch the intestines back in more carefully, little by little, as they are very sensitive to cold, and so they will swell up and cause more pain if stitched quickly; and so it is better to treat a minor wound by gradually replacing the intestines to their proper place, rather than all at once. And know that there are four types of rupture: two common types occur in stomach stitching, and the stitching of other wounds on the body; and two proper types are unique to other wounds. And yet they are more proper with stomach stitching, and I will explain each in turn.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and something of the intestines has come out, and a greased object is used to push it back in, this is done by one of two methods: either due to the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in such a way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in warm water only, or cook it in water with squill and cypress and spices, and wipe the intestines until the swelling is gone; and sometimes this wine restraint is made, and it is solely for deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling leaving, moisten the intestines with water or old wine in which mallows and mulberries have been cooked, for there is a tightness in the entrance due to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small slit in the wound with the instrument used to scrape out hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than cutting, which one must not do without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: cut into the curve and push outward, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, then put them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is low on the belly, you should have the patient lie on his back with his legs elevated higher than his head; and if it is high up on the belly, then he should be flat on his back with his head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture in the belly is to one side, then the injured part should be elevated higher than the other; and thus you should arrange things as I say for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have at hand; then take a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, and leave an inch of space from the top of the wound, and pierce through both sides of the skin and the subcutaneous tissue beneath with a needle so that it comes out the other side; then tie off the thread around the needle, and pull the two sides of the wound together gently, leaving another inch of space, and insert another needle; then tie off the thread again as before, and continue doing this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is closed up. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, so they can pierce through the skin and flesh without reopening the wound; then bend the ends of the needles so they don't poke the patient when sleeping, and put some tents or bandages over the needle heads to hold them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed. This type of suturing with needles is best for small wounds, as there is less risk of reopening the wound. I also sewed up a man's wound on his belly with this method; it had been cut with a knife, and the intestines were hanging out two inches from the wound, which was larger than a palm.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back to health after his intestine had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they looked at him and thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I didn't treat him with ointment because I was in a place where there were no ointments or any medicine; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
