Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about two proper ways to sew: take the needle and pierce it from one side of the wound into the other; as soon as it has pierced the skin directly from right to right, then hold it with your fingers where you have just pierced it with the needle, and pierce it again on the other side of the wound until it comes out on the other side. The technique of this sewing is that you sew like a tailor sews pelts, leaving a flap of skin on one side, and then pulling it from the other, until the seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: take two pieces of thread and tie them together naturally, then apply one end of the thread to the other, in such a way that an needle is inserted near the wound's edge and only pierces through the skin on one side, leaving the two edges of the wound untouched; then turn the needle and pierce through from the outside, into the inside, at both edges of the wound; finally, pierce through from the outside to the inside at two other points along the wound's edge, on the opposite side, and tie off. This is the best and most common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen describes this procedure and some testify that one must stitch the abdomen with two needles, each with its own thread; then, one needle is pushed from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew leather. Know that when the incision is in the lower abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the burn has moved it, then put back the intestines and the skin; then put on the powder of the ointment, and if the burn has moved, put on some ointment that is present until the wound heals; then cut the threads, and sew up the lips, and the mirror; then cure the wound as with the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, then put on old cotton immediately when it begins to heal, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine for various dispositions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause community in the principal members, then you should wet light wool in tempered oil, or rose oil, and put it around the anus, and under the buttocks; and if there is pain or porridge in the bowels, and it happens many times, then cleanse them with a warm black wine enema, and likewise if the porridge comes all the way to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called 'young', cannot heal when they are injured, and this is due to the thinness of the veins through which they run, and the subtlety of the entire body, and their close connection to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the vein pops out of the wound, then put it back in as you would with the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must tie off the area that is black so that no blood flow comes to it, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends down from below the wound until it eases out when the vein breaks, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the route of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are pierced and the wound is small, then one can restore it in some people, for I saw a man who was wounded in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became an abscess, and from it came digestion and flatulence; I applied a poultice according to what I could, and did not cease subtilizing until he was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewing up the wound, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain but stayed in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in this way: take a thread from a ram's testicles, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it over the two lips so that it tightens his mouth shut; then tie off the thread, and it will stay like that so that he cannot undo it, then put another thread after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and then cut the thread.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these wounds are in the intestine and do not cause any harm to the patient, one can sew up the intestine with a thin thread cut from an animal's intestine in this way: take the end of this intestinal thread which is very sinewy, then tie to it a thin twisted linen thread; then thread the needle and sew up the wound, and draw it tight at the end; and this method of sewing with threads is only useful according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the graily intestines, there is nothing that can be done about it.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is hooded and bowed in.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green knot, hard and white, where there is no pain, and is as hooded as the beak of a bird; sometimes it is clear bowing, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large; I have spoken about these causes in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no flesh inside, except for one of nine causes: namely, due to thinness of blood or body; or because of evilness; or because there is hard matter within it, and on the lips, that does not allow pus to form; or if there is too much pus; or if the site is wounded and the matter poor in quality; or if the medicine is not good for the treatment; or because corruption is a type of pestilence; or because digestion and healing are slow by nature, and swollen; or if there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicinal treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is done with the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the sinus, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and they also occur in parts that come from the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of a grievous nature, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the places I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it, then take a tent of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, so take it; and if the fistula is crooked, then seek it with a thin tent of lead, for the lead bends easily around the crook; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly seek it with tents, then enema through one of the openings, for moisture cuts from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then press it hard, to the best of your ability, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and see if it is deep-seated and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the location and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned, then treat it according to what I have told you, and remove the rotten flesh and corruption that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you should treat it deeply, as much as you can, then place moist tents in medicine water, and insert them into the chief of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments to promote healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then treat it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve troubles the principal limbs as we have said, and if there is decay and blackness in the bone, let the king treat it until all decay is removed; then cure it with healing things while it is being healed; and if it is not healed, return bow-wise as before, know that you have not yet reached the bottom; then uncover and seek until you reach the bottom, and remove all decay, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, you know that the decay is too deep for you to reach it; then there is nothing else to do but let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone decayed and you can pull it out with tweezers, or extract it with a suitable instrument for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out one by one; and if moisture causes a contrary effect, and there is no error or fear, then cut and dry and heal.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something on the wound to draw out pus, and let it remain until the swelling has spread around the bone, and then the bones will come loose more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, then draw out the corruption only as far as the darkness, and then dress the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption, and it extends to the soft tissue of the bone, then one must scrape away and cover up the whole area until the corruption is removed, and then heal the wound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from an internal cause, so that the matter came out through the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but they miraculously worked on it until the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared from which pus and moisture poured out from his body; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, so that I was called to see him, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the openings was a great harm to his body; and the skin of the young man turned red, and he had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came against another all the way down the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened therefore, and probed one of the openings until I exposed a portion of the bone, and found it corrupt and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone within; I removed what appeared to me to be of the bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had removed; and then I began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but could not close it; so I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and removed it, and then closed up the place; but I could not heal it as much as I probed around a palm of the bone, and drew it out completely to its very marrow, then healed it with medicines; and it was healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to repeat the operation except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the bloodletting, he often bled profusely, but he was completely healed, and in the bone a hard lump grew, and he had a good disposition and no harm or contrary effect anywhere, neither lying nor moving.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be bound in this way: take a bandage and tie it at the top of the open bone, and command someone to pull it upwards; and put another larger woolen bandage over the hard lump that is on the bone, and bind it at the top, so that you draw out the corrupted flesh from below and uncover the flesh where one can see and feel the corruption, and bind it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh everywhere; then place a burning brand underneath, and then draw out the corruption from one side to the other, and let the incision be as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut through the corrupted joint, and draw out the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other way but to cut it; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or the knuckle of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire into this corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in every way you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not cause any harm; and know that there are many types of cutting instruments for covering these bones, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness. And therefore one must prepare a tool for each type of work; and know that the craft will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; then choose the tool you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head can become dislocated due to internal causes or external forces. And when you have treated this injury with remedies but they do not help, then cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion occurs so that the patient escapes death, or the greater harm, from the defect in the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and then it turns red under the blackness, and this corrosion spreads from limb to limb throughout the body. If it is caused by the sting of some venomous creature, such as a sea scorpion or snake, and the injury is on the head, then cover it and give it no space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then it is fatal, and there is no remedy but to reduce the amount of poison according to its virulence. And this is how you cover a limb: you bind it above and below with bands, and extend one band downward, and another band upward, and you separate the flesh that is between the two bands with a spatumile as wide as possible so that the bone is exposed; then cover it with a linen cloth on both sides so that the cloth does not touch the healthy area, and bring the patient another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the wound thoroughly or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete. Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it heals. I will tell you what happened to a man on his foot: he developed a darkness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe on his foot, spreading throughout his foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he wrapped his foot, and it healed. A long time after, the corrosion reappeared on his fingers, and he came to me, and I placed some reflective substances on him after cleansing his body, but I could not stop the corrosions. He wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to do so because I had hope of driving out the matter. I was also afraid that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak. He despaired completely, returned home, wrapped his hand, and healed; and I have never heard of anyone else doing this who needed it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in a fleshy area, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it erupts and pierces, and the pus flows out, leaving the spot hollow like a vessel; the skin above is as delicate as a torn cloth, and does not heal all the way to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'sore', and is not called a 'fistula'; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called a 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can cover it all around, and especially when it is delicate, like a cloth; and it does not heal by formation of scar tissue.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the skin is healing, and the corruption is not deep, and the flesh is thick, then he is treated with a clyster as follows: examine whether the breast is swollen, and the pus which comes from it has an offensive odor, then clyster with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take equal parts of aloe, oil, and litharge, and put them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and clyster the breast and tighten the orifice; leave it for two hours, then extract it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is healed and the pus is eliminated; and sometimes one is clystered with ashes of vine wood when this medicine is not available, and it is done thus: collect ashes of vine wood and pour water over them, then strain and clyster with it, until you know that the breast is cleaned; if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then clyster with water and honey in which there is a little litharge powder; or you clyster with honey and wine in which the honey has properties of cleaning and washing, and the wine causes the sore to dry up; and when you have done this and you are confident that the breast is cleaned, then clyster with something that causes flesh to grow in it, and take diaphoretic plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you clyster with other medicines and ointments of which I have spoken of their properties in the section on ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle, and put in some Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, as far as it can reach; and if the wound is too large, then cut and leave only the part where the clyster can enter, and if the opening which discharges pus is above, then cover it or lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowels are in perfect health, one should not let Char enter; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, prepare in such a way that the bowels move to the lowest place they can, for when the bowels are in perfect health, one should not let Char enter, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, prepare in such a way: that the bowels move slightly downward, and leave nothing of the bowels; and take consolidating medicines to put over the wound, and they must be on top of a linen drape that covers all the wound; then cover the most forceable place of the breast opening more widely than before, then apply an ointment according to the quantity of the opening, and place it over the opening of the wound to alleviate the bowels, and do not remove the large drape for many days at a time; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels, whether it is venom, pus, or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that emerges over the opening of the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and approaching health; and then loosen it in the morning, or in the middle of the day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows in an unripe state after several days, know that the breast will not produce milk.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread over a long time, you should not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose flesh slowly decays in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if indigested food rises from the stomach after many days, know that it does not settle; and if it takes a long time for the stomach to settle and is distant, then apply dry medicines which are moist in substance but dry in virtue, like diaphanous ointment, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and it is the best medicine; take diaphanous ointment and make it with rose oil, and rose water equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and if you do not have diaphanous ointment ready, take myrrh, aloes, and incense, and grind them into powder over the honey when it is on the fire; then glue a cloth to it, and place it over the stomach, and sometimes one administers Aristologus for a long time, and roots of the celestial lily, which is like wheat flour and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them and make them into powder, and put them onto the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the fistula is slow to heal and is not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep, and it makes impressions in the bone, or in the hard limbs, or in the tissues; so do the cure of fistulas as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaris is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or it may appear elsewhere; and when it becomes infected, and no action is taken, an abscess forms, and it grows and extends to the root of the nail, and sometimes even further; and erosion reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the area around the digit becomes swollen, and the color turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you should cut away all the excess tissue that is hanging from the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is very effective if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail begins to grow into the flesh, and the edge starts to blister, then you should place a thread beneath the nail so that it lifts the flesh, and tie it tightly above, and carefully cut away the dead tissue, and apply burning and corrosive medications to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and draw it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see that it is corrupted, cut it on both sides of the nail as previously described, then cure it until it heals; and if it is raw and bleeding, and he feels great pain, you must treat him first; then cut the nail of the finger斜 at an angle from above, and be careful not to cut into the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel great pain; and if this happens, put something over it to soothe the wound.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deaf person's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that grow in some people's hands by chance are sometimes all flesh, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes nails; and some grow from the root of the joint, and the growth is on some fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in the head of the jaw do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the jaw may move; the size of the one who is fleshy is slight, in such a way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the root of the joint are difficult to cure; you must cover them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those who are born in the back of the jaw, you should first scrape the round flesh to the bone, then scrape the bone with an appropriate needle, then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Joints can be united by birth, or by the joining of a wound, or by a burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you should scrape that seam so that the jaws fit together according to their natural shapes; then put between two tents or moistened sheets in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or put between two pieces of subtle plaster, until the jaw is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If adhesion occurs to one of his hands with the palm, correct that adhesion as it should be.
des vils	of the evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Wens are large, wrapped tumors full of melancholy superfluities, which come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him some purgative medicine, and then the basil drink.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure with iron is in two ways: one is that you cut and draw out the black blood; the other way is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cure with incision is in this way: first heat the leg in very hot water until the large vessels are subtilized, then stretch the leg from above the thigh to the part under the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places, with a wide incision, then open and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the medication can tolerate; then tie it off and command that he eat foods mixed with black gall; and begin the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and repeat the treatment.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the disease is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and warm the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then press the vein from the top to the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the nail, and scrape the vein on each side until it appears when one feels it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then tie it under the vein, so that it is lifted from the skin, and then it can be easily tied at another nail; then make another cut, or several if you need to, then lift it and press it on the toe, then draw and lift it up to the second cut; then pull it out of the cuts one by one until it comes out completely, then tie it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a strong doubled thread with a needle, tie it and pull it, and insert it under the vein, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and be careful that it does not rip, because if it rips, one cannot pull and lift it, and it brings harm to the patient; and when you have treated it completely, place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the bone is bent and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one splits the bone must be curved, and it must not cut so that it does not split the vein; and it must be a gross curve because if it were thin it would split the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of a civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is jagged in the legs, in warm parts where herbs or trees do not grow, and in land where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from porridge that comes underneath the skin, just as snakes and worms come inside the body, jaggedy between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	If the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the location changes, and the wound begins to come out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound opens, you should wrap around it a piece of cloth two and a half yards to three yards long, and tie it, leaving the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time it comes out, wrap it around the cloth again, and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the rest, but do not cover its root until it all comes out; because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and pus in the wound, which is bad; therefore, this wound should be treated a little bit at a time until it is fully healed, and nothing remains in the body; sometimes this wound can be as long as five or ten palms, one man came to me whose was ten palms long, when you cover it, pierce the tip or opening with a needle all the way to the bottom so that everything comes out, then empty the matter inside, and administer healing medicines on subsequent days, then treat it like any other abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or at the foot itself, and it gushes out copiously, and from which it sprinkles blood; treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that live between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "buef" in our land because it often affects oxen. It is caused by a small worm that lives between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks out of the skin wherever it goes, and it sprinkles blood; and it is due to the putrefaction of certain humors, just as worms, snakes, earthworms, and roundworms live in the belly. One fears its malice because when it moves through the body and ascends to the head, it can enter and destroy the eye; this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn out, one cannot help but wince when it goes: so therefore you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then press on it and draw it out forcefully; and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not draw it out, cauterize it with fire until it comes out; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, then tightly constrict under it the eyelid, then press on it and draw it out forcefully; and one should use the cleansing of the body with solutive medicines to remove bad humors, and a diet of warming foods to promote suppuration.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called 'wind-pain' in our language, and it is a pain that afflicts certain members, then moves from member to member; I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman and she uncovered her arm and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her elbow; and then soon after, I saw it rise up her shoulder like a worm, more quickly than anything, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in her shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout her body, until it reached her other arm; then she told me she felt it circulating around her body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how it moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this disease progress in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many people whose pain moved from one place to another, but I have not seen it as clearly as in this woman; and I believed that it was because women's bodies are drier, and their veins are more exposed, and thus the wind finds an easy passage; but it does not appear in those who are plump and have moist skin and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease being treated and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then ligature above and below tightly, and then press on it until that windiness forced out of its place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat by those who dislodge windiness, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The varieties of them are that there are some with large points, and small, and hooked, and blunt; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and one which breaks in any member breaks according to two ways: either in a principal member it breaks, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it therefore occurs in any part of these limbs and the sign of death that I will tell you about later becomes apparent to you: then you should take care to extract this arrow, for death comes afterwards in various ways; and when this bad sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of death when the arrow pierces the bone and hits the brain, is when there is bleeding and pus coming from the nose or ears, and also swelling and redness in these parts, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of blood; and perhaps a discharge from the nose or ears; and sometimes they lose their speech and voice; and from the wound there is white moisture that resembles pus, and it seeps out like the breath of a fire, and there is also a bruise-like discoloration around the wound; and if this sign becomes apparent to you, then stop the treatment and pull out the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a seizure when it occurs in the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as though it were pierced by a hard object, not hollow; and sometimes the seizure is silent like the pulse, and black blood flows, and there is a chill and cold sweat, and a fainting: then know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves the lung is that without pain foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits in the covering of the foot, it is between the small ribs; and there is great swelling and great pain and breathing; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something undigested will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow hits the belly, and nothing comes out of the bowel but feces, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow hits the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain, know that this wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and hip and thigh and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There was once a man who had a seizure in the jaw, and it fell into the roots of his teeth; I treated it by stretching it from under the ear fat, and he recovered without loss of consciousness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And on a boy there was a seizure that fell into the fat of the eye under the paper under the lower jaw; and the seizure was drawn back, and he could only reach it with the tip towards the body, and the seizure was as big as a Turkish arrowhead, all iron-hard without ears; the boy recovered, and no bad accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow to the ears; I lanced the abscesses, and I extracted it gently, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I extracted an arrow from a man's home, which was lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve; so I cut into the arrow, and cauterized it, and pulled it out, and he had no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man whom an arrow has pierced in the back, and the wound is sewn up on top of it; and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions remain unchanged, and he finds no harm in any of his natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man whom an arrow had hit in the face, and his wound was sewn up; and he remained like that without experiencing great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And drew an arrow at the home of the princes the king, who had a toothache in his jaw, and was slightly declining to the right side; and the arrow was all swollen I was called to the cure after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I wanted to probe it with a very thin instrument, and I didn't feel anything; but he felt piercing and pain under his right ear.Je le queris alerge les deux oreilles et la gueule, et il le voudroit point faire; car il estoit sain home.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed a healing and digestive poultice on the site to reduce swelling; and I saw the tip of the arrow.Et si me prier, que je le traisse; et je ne voulus point faire, por ceu qu’il estoit sain home, si ne fu pour alerger les oreilles et la gueule.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice again after a few days, and the wound healed again, but the patient felt the arrow in his jaw for a long time; he told me about it.Et si me demanda se li seroien venuz as oreilles, car il sentoit l’esgout de la saiette dedens ses oreilles et sa gueule.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open and I could feel the head of the arrow which was lodged there; then I treated the wound with the medicine until the head of the arrow became visible; the wound healed well within four months, and then I lanced it, probing with tweezers from both sides but unable to extract anything; so I continued to probe and manipulate with instruments until one day I was able to grasp it with specially made tweezers, as described in this chapter, and I removed the arrowhead and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And I saw that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; so I restored it, closed the wound, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Here I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your treatment on what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters reason well on very small things, and on what is present and lacking to them, they devise new works and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that come to this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows grow from the members where they are stuck in two ways: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and those that go out by the place where they entered are arrows entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes they go out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not go out now, then leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes putrid and the passageway is cleared; and also, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce through to the very tip of a subtle forest, as long as the passages around it are widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and penetrates one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the symptoms I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not extract it, but let it be until it becomes even with some part of the skin, for if the arrow reaches the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for several days without any bad symptoms, then treat it by extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck deeply and cannot be removed, then administer cauterization around it, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged deeply in the body so that it cannot be seen, then probe it throughout; and if you feel it, extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then cut around the wound to make it larger; and if there are barbs on the arrow that hold it in place, remove the shaft as far as you can, and then bend or twist the barbs of the arrow so that you can extract it; be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, then leave it until the flesh around it is swollen, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.
