And if the flow of blood makes it contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of incision into the nerve and of opening a vein, and put oil as you are able to move the arrow without peril, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to how he was when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Arrows that come from another direction, or where something is sticking out of them, or the skin is swollen in that area, if one can see it or feel it apparently: cut above it, as far as the tweezers can grab it, and then pull it out; if it won't come out just yet.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is caught in the bone, then rotate your hand rapidly, so that it goes into the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for now and try again to extract it; and if there is a fragment of the arrow inside, then insert the instrument as far as the shaft; and if the shaft is broken, and you see that administration of the instrument is possible, then administer the instrument with its point entering in so as to облегчить extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched, then you must cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the buttock or thigh or belly or bladder or side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut around it, then do so; but be careful not to cut into the vein and nerve, and then pull out the arrow, and then stitch up the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of tweezers used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like that of a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, just as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tweezers to pull and to check if it is there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins that can be used for bleeding, and they have 16 openings in the head: two just behind the ears, called "ear-veins"; and the two arteries in the temples that are visible; and two veins in the corners of the eyes, called "sight-veins"; and the vein in the middle of the forehead; and the vein at the base of the nose; and the two windpipes that are in the neck; and the two veins on the upper lip, which are called "upper-lip veins"; and the two veins underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	Veins, which are commonly used for healing, are V in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it 'vein of the head'; and the middle one is called 'fast', composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it 'vein of the heart'; and the basilic vein is on the right side of the chest, and the common people call it 'vein of the belly', and it is above the cubital fossa, and it is the one used for healing, which opens clearly above the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvator vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has II branches; and in the leg there are III veins: one is below the bend of the left-side pocket, and the second sophene which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called  'nesse', which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are III veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrhs and by emigration; and the qualities of the bleedings, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then stretch the patient's neck to a vise, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head; then press them to your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, sign with ink; then take the lance, and pierce it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein upstream, and pierce both the skin and the vein well with two thrusts, and make the blood come out until you see it; then stretch and tie it, so that it is healed; and I have already spoken of the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries in the temples, if it helps to cure old blindness and blindness due to cataracts, and tears in the eyes, and the body of ague in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as I said: and that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, and then sign with your finger; then lift the vein above your finger to the top, and insert the needle underneath, and lift the vein above, and cup it, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as effective as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for migraines and redness; and its quality is such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called a "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein and press up with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see; then loosen the neck of the patient, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the operation is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not right that the flames be too sharp; and the sick person should not move about, because the bone is close by, and perhaps the flames will break when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples helps with earaches and eye pains, and with redness and migraines; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting some part of it, as before; then bleed him, and let the bleeding be through the vein, a little from the long flame a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they may break; then make an incision to draw blood, as much as you need, and then bind it on a cotton pad, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein-bleeding for the nose is good for aguishness and for sudden madness and for face-sickness, such as мигрень and redness that comes in the face, and also when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient holds his neck, then pulls on his nose with his left hand, takes a long, thin flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it for one night, for it is quickly restored. And this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two veins helps with swelling in the throat, and with the beginning of toothache, and with many illnesses, and with empyema, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and with estiomata; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient holds his neck from side to side, as we have said; and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein of the arm widely for a little, then draw the blood gently, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and gently pinch both veins so that the patient does not choke; and let him stay until the morning, so that the wound can heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins in the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and pain in the teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of bleeding is to have the patient sit before you and stretch his neck as I said; then turn up the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be distinguished by their being black, and by there being around them fine black veins: pinch both, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt, then pinch the largest of each side, and likewise do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same technique.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that are beneath the tongue is helped after the bleeding of the cephalic vein; it is due to constriction of the throat, and illnesses of the eye, and illnesses of the mouth; the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun, and lift up his tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: treat both, and do not go too deep, because beneath them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either with a wide, pointed mirtin twig, or with a thin olive-wood skewer, and it is called 'anesil'; they are wide and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame of myrtle is highly renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the flat veins that contain thick and apparent blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood; this is the shape of the olive-wood skewer:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, used for bleeding veins that are fine and contain subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and the surgeon must bleed it cleanly, and bandage the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it pierces the artery, and blood flows out, then it must be stopped as I have said; and the flame should not be gripped, but cut off like a candle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic does not open obviously, then you must stretch it and change to another; or you can bleed in its place through the arm: it will open obviously; and grip the flame at the end, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to find the location for bleeding, then you must stretch the arm and feel for the pulse; then mark the spot, and then tie the arm, and pierce the vein at the end of the flame, and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see it pulsing, for that is the artery: avoid it therefore.Et se li sangs estainche, et tu vees que il ne vout point, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et tu cope l’artere sus la voinne, et puis tu saine dou flaime; ou tu quieres rain d’en la voinne, ou tu saine en leu de li, car c’est li meins sainable.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising upward like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that this is the blood of an artery: therefore hasten, and place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, as often happens; tie the arm and leave it thus, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched and he bleeds and medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for that is where the blood comes from; and staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fir-bark, and split it, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then stop it with a cautery, as we have said, using powders to stop bleeding; and the stopping of bleeding is not harmful in various conditions because of the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps it to draw blood from both above and below, because it is composed of basil and cedar, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful not to pierce the nerve underneath, and if he pierces too deeply, and finds the nerve, it will swell and become injured, and may never heal; and this nerve often appears, and if in some men it does not appear because of its subtlety, then you must stop it with an instrument; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, they cut it open.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes; and one should bleed with a flame of olive oil or a flame of myrrh, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest vein, and not worry if one misses the first time, and try again; and perhaps the site will swell in some people if one misses the first time, but it will not hurt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding depends on your thought process.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only done to maintain health and prevent diseases; and bleeding should be done in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the superficial temporal, and the basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but when there is a need during the day or night, at all hours and at all times; and children should not be bled until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus beyond the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very elderly who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when one wishes to bleed, in any manner, they should first cleanse the intestines with a gentle clyster if they have retained much waste, so that the veins are not drawn from the intestines by harmful superfluities damaging the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are too full from eating meat, or who are drunk, as long as they remain so, nor the very elderly, nor those suffering from dropsy; and one should not bleed after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, and excessive sexual activity in women, nor from exertion, watching, fasting, and what weakens the body, either through arms or the rest of the body; then subtly draw out the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicine if you have the skill; then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein around the wrist, as we have said; and guard against exertion that day, and from pain, and excess, and similar things; and be calm and cheerful, and let the person bleeding be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature gently, for if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot draw the blood; then rub the site with the hand two or three times until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the needle with a little old oil, then press their thumb of their left hand against the vein below where they wish to bleed, so that the vein does not slip away from the needle.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords in the body, and some are filled with wind, so that when one applies a flame, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein; and thus one finds these. And if one opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeon must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein works the first time, that is good; if not, do it again a little lower down on that spot or higher up, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the arm is swollen and the patient is in fear, if one leaves it for a day or two and does not bind the arm: perhaps a cold abscess will develop; do not enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if she wishes; and if the opening is small, cut the skin around the vein subtly and gently, and if you doubt that enough blood will flow as you wish, then apply the flame directly to that opening; and work quickly, so that the arm is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swelling, do not re-open the wound, and put a little linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is turned into liniment; and thus administer liniment to every wound that you open veins, to stop the flow of blood; and it does the same when applied to триачель and bowels, when it is put on the spot; it gently draws out the blood and disperses it when it is too abundant.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not bled before the opening of the vein is small, you must act quickly and put a sponge soaked in warm water and salt on the spot and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein has stopped, and if a blackness or greenness remains in the spot after a few days, it does no harm; and if you see any swelling, put something made from aloe or myrrh reduced to juice, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and swelling at the exit of the urethra; therefore place your hand upon it, and if you feel the spot soft to the touch under pressure, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid putting anything of what we have said upon it, for perhaps it will go away without any artery being involved; but make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then treat the wound with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and the strength of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, that they make a larger wound, and the flames should be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they should bleed little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not piercing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding from a long or wide wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is good to give them wet bread in pomegranate juice; if they are hot-tempered, bleed them three or four times. And if of a cold complexion, eat moist bread before bleeding, dipped in spiced honey syrup, or in aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after losing a lot of blood, then he should drink warm broth and fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the chapter on syncope, for opening the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by a large bleed, that he bleeds little by little according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to open their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, then heal for .7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, then they should bleed on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a lot of blood inside the body that has been heated, and it causes fever; so you must draw off a large quantity, and widen the hole until it bleeds freely; then you should check all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come to the part where the vein is, and this happens many times when the bloodletting is négligent. And if when you see the arm loosening and the blood coming out a second time, and the hole is closed, you must not press directly on it; nor if it is crooked, should he stretch his arm forcefully, for that would be bad. Instead, let it bleed until it is finished bleeding for the second time, then touch the tip of the wound with a flame, so that the congealed blood at the opening of the vein melts away, and apply a little salt in water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is reduced.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to let blood a second time, then bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healthy in the area of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is for the patient to put his hand in warm water until the vein turns red; then let it be tied loosely so that the vein appears well, and then bleed immediately through the middle, not through the width or length; and let the incision be wide, and let the bleeding be done close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand in warm water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is in winter, do not re-immerse the hand in warm water, because it is more immersed in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the back of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: stretch out the hand and put it in warm water until the vein swells; if you can see it, then bleed through the middle, and if you close it all the way around, it will do no harm; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are completely naked under the skin, and then put the hand back in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have stopped the bleeding as much as necessary, then put oil and silk on the wound to heal quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and do everything just as I told you about the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophia is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the stomach, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and the buttocks and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are such that the patient puts it in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it pops out, and then he applies it to the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot, they should move a lot of fluids; therefore treat it either at the largest vein or at the ankle, whichever moves more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it at the foot, then be careful of the nerves underneath, and cut it across as well as up and down; and let the flames go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the salve fails the first time, do it again the second time, for the site is salty; do not be afraid of nerves as we have said, and likewise do with the sophia on the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle bone, and its pulsation extends to the pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his healing is that the patient enters the bath, and twists the ankle three times upwards, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cup it, for the site is safe, and it is very relaxing for many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not drain it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make the blood flow until you see enough, and then loosen the ligature and put on cotton and tighten it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horn, or bronze, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this venesection which is done by burning is done in two ways: with or without fire; and venesection which is done by burning and by bloodletting is done in 14 places of the body, of which one is on the top of the head; and the other is in the neck; and two others are on either side of the neck; and the cupping is under the chin; and the cupping is on the shoulders; and the cupping is on the hips; and the cupping is on the buttocks; and the cupping is on the thighs; and the cupping is on the calves; and the cupping is on the ankles; and venesection does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as is done with bloodletting; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary to bleed due to illness or habit, we should do so at the beginning or end of the month, and in all seasons; for there are some who, when they need to bleed, experience a heavy head, and some who become congested and red in the face, head, and neck, and darken their eyes; and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and swell their tongue, and taste blood; and there are those who faint, and see blackness and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it occurs during the night, we instruct them to drink a medicine after three hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches ... that come from the eyes, and it must not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this bleeding is in place of the cephalic bleeding, and it must not be used by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and because of this the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal from it become oblate, and because of this, the cupping glasses should be placed a little lower down due to the risk of oblateness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Ventilation in the neck is located at the junction of the head and basilic vein, and for this reason it helps with constriction of the feet, and with fissures in the channels of the lungs, and with constipation and distension; and one should not push on it too much, because if held too firmly it can cause damage to the oesophagus, stomach, and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation holes at the back of the neck help with headaches and migraines, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and are located where the basilic vein opens; and you must instruct the surgeon to hold his hand while inserting, so that he does not press on the artery and cause a gushing of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; it is in the location of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the armpits is good for a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation holes in the armpits are like three veins in the arm, as they draw blood from these large vessels; and instruct the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, because under the skin there are nerves and arteries.Li ventosations dou poing atrait sanc des bras et des coutes; li sainors covient qu’il les fasse a la fin de l’operation, qu’il ne fiet avant, car il est leus des ners qui vont a li membres.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is placed on the hip is good for hemorrhoids and diseases underneath; and the cupping glass should be large and made of copper, which it needs to draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping on the legs heal very well, for they draw blood from throughout the body, and are effective for long-standing pains in the kidneys, and the bladder, and for hernia; and they bring relief to swelling in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is to first apply it empty, and suck gently, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the color of blood appears; then release, and re-apply the cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those with thin skin and clear pores: thus one should only pierce once, and make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, one should pierce twice: the first time to subtilize the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, one should pierce a third time; and when we want to draw blood a little at a time, we only pierce once.Et se li sans est maigre, et les porez clers, si covient ferir tres foiz: car il ne peut sortir tout le gros sans que la voie ne soit subtiliée par traison du sang maigre.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we should bleed often; and if the blood is thick, pierce it with a needle, and heat the tip so that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is appropriate for those who have tough, hard skin and tight pores to anoint the spots where the cupping glasses will be placed with an aperitif and dissolutive oil: if it is in the summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, use watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or of fennel, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one is being bled from tender skin and large pores, then no oil should be used, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should get up from garlic, or myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large swellings should rise from old wine, or from water of suckling, or from the decoction of fennel or camomile, or from other such things; and one must not bleed with a cupping-glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and one must not sleep after bloodletting, and one must be careful when one is to be bled and when one has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the person being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed; one must eat cool things, like pomegranates and endive and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and drink little, and eat charred food from a pot, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cool complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderate old wine, and eat moist food, and drink little, and eat small birds and pigeons; and on the day one is bled, one should drink more than one eats; and one should give some men treacle or muscate before bloodletting, or afterwards, to comfort the principal members; and the blood should be subdued, but those who are hot-tempered should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are used for bleeding are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the gout, and on the belly and the buttocks, and the thighs, and the hips; because these members do not endure being hurt on the eyes, and it is not done except to draw blood from one member to another, as we put them on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the member; and it removes pain when there is inflammation or stone, or by its attractive power it removes the inflammation, or drives out the stone from its place; and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the mumps when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it is two digits wide and a half palm deep, and on the side around the middle there is a small hole, just big enough to push through a needle, and it should be made of bronze, smooth in front so that it does not bleed the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of bronze or iron, for holding a candle, and they are both large and small according to the illnesses and ages of those who use them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this ventouse on the limb: take the candle of wax or the liniment, and put it inside the ventouse through the crossbar, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be over the hole we mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapor will go, and one removes the ventouse; then take the liniment as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse which is administered for pleurisy, all types of aiguë, there is no tube or aperture, and it is not removed until it is filled with water, and is placed on the affected member by itself. And that is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not removed until they are in soft, clean water without any dirt, and they are placed on members where you cannot place ventouses due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on bare flesh, such as toes or fingers, and others; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in soft, clean water without dirt, you take them; and put them in a bowl of soft water until they are familiar with it, and have nothing in their bellies; and then they should be bled from a vein and with a ventouse, then rub the affected member until it is red, and place the leeches on top of it; and when they are full and start to bite, if there is a place where one can place a ventouse, one should do so, for that helps a lot.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the affected area above the level of the heart, and then above water, very well, and then compress it; and if the bite marks are too low on the body, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it over the bite until the swelling is reduced; and if the bites are numerous, apply powdered vitriol, or gall, and similar substances, until the swelling is reduced; or place half a handful of peeled peas over the bite, and leave them there until they warm up to the bite, and it will stop bleeding immediately; and if you need more, take more leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the leeches will not attach, then rub the bite with fresh blood, or prick the area with a needle until blood comes out, and then apply them, and as soon as they taste the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are excreting, then sprinkle powdered aloe and salt, or ash, over them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a cure for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people wonder at this chapter, for they have never seen it in any of the ancient books nor read any letter in it; and because of this, knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found any good in it; and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have gained knowledge, and by experience and the habit of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the subjects of the discussion and the chapters in which the sage sets his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs in someone, you should hurry to heal the patient from one side and another if nothing else stops it, such as weakness of the body, or old age, or youth; or if the weather is not very hot or too cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cool meat, and deer and goat meat, and do not drink any wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have a doubt about a hot abscess or swelling of matter in the limb; then return the patient to their previous way of life.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one must feed the patient foods that promote swelling and stickiness, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, and offal, and fresh fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with this swelling the bones will close up and heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well healed or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but have no concern, reset the broken bone with the large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, so that it enforces it as it was before; and do not stop completely from his work, and for this reason one should eat plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracturing.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in grinding, as with the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all over a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner, there is its own skill and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory comes into its place; and it is known that there is a fracture of the bone by the fact that the area is twisted, and appears well by displacement, and sounds on pressure with the hand; and when there is no twisting or pain on touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but there can be twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it by hand, but rather apply the remedies that follow, and then hold it firmly in place.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes into the bone, and are the two parts separated, they must now be set even, so that the abscesses heal; and if hot abscesses come, then let it rest for a day, until the abscess is relieved; then set it even with the movements you can make easily and without pain, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of the one who has pieces; then bind it as it should be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is in two parts, whether it is arm or leg, or a hand, if it is a small member, or two tendons, or one tendon and a hand; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, they are pulled by all means into their places with the movements you can make easily and without pain, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and join the two ends of the bone well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then dress it nicely, and do not pull or press too hard as those who cause hot abscesses and contraction in the limb by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its worst, then treat the patient carefully so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or otherwise; and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not at its worst, and it must be put in such a position that he feels no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and similar: these should be wrapped with soft, fine linen; and for larger ones, such as thigh and leg, use a wide, firm bandage, as the wide bandages embrace the whole large member and constrict it equally all around, so that there is no gap; then wind light-weight bandages around three or four times according to the member, and press your hand gently on all the bandage, then go above the fracture and constrict less, so that the fracture is drawn out a little; then soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it directly over the broken area; then return to the part below the fracture and constrict gently, not too tightly or too loosely, as we said in the first hour above; then place bandages of linen or cloth between the bandages so that they are all even, then tie a bandage over everything, and then apply your splints well made over it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place a hot poultice to soothe the abscess and reduce the swelling, leaving it for several days; then apply a compress made from half a length of a large cane, cut to bleed, or from palm fronds, shaped in this manner:
